                response = xhr.response;
            }

                            if(trial.reportInDataLayer){
                                var usedCredits = trial.totalCredits - trial.remainingCredits
                                if (window.Zephr.groupFields && !pageView.zephrTrials) pageView.zephrTrials = {};
                                var target = window.Zephr.groupFields ? pageView.zephrTrials : pageView

                                }
                                if (trial.dataLayerCreditsRemainingKey) {
                                   target[trial.dataLayerCreditsRemainingKey] = trial.remainingCredits;
                                }
                            }
                        });
                        (window.Zephr.accessDetails.trialTrackingDetails || []).forEach(function(details) {
                            var type = details.entitlementType === 'credits' ? 'credits' : 'meters';
                            var trial = (window.Zephr.accessDetails[type] || {})[details.entitlementId];
                            if (!trial) return;
                            if (window.Zephr.groupFields && !pageView.zephrTrials) pageView.zephrTrials = {};
                            if (details.creditsRemainingKey) {
                                if (window.Zephr.groupFields) {
                                    pageView.zephrTrials[details.creditsRemainingKey] = trial.remainingCredits;
                                } else {
                                    pageView[details.creditsRemainingKey] = trial.remainingCredits;
                                }
                            }
                            if (details.creditsUsedKey) {
                                if (window.Zephr.groupFields) {
                                    pageView.zephrTrials[details.creditsUsedKey] = trial.totalCredits - trial.remainingCredits;
                                } else {

                                }
                            }
                        });

            <h3 class="PagePromo-title">
                <a class="Link " href="https://apnews.com/article/saturday-night-live-snl-50th-jean-smart-9205f31f0eab80700604f39581b84cf3"><span class="PagePromoContentIcons-text">‘Saturday Night Live’ launches 50th season with Jean Smart, Jelly Roll and maybe Maya as Kamala</span></a>
            </h3>
        </bsp-custom-headline>
    





        



    <div class="PagePromo-description">
        <a class="Link " href="https://apnews.com/article/saturday-night-live-snl-50th-jean-smart-9205f31f0eab80700604f39581b84cf3"><span class="PagePromoContentIcons-text">“Saturday Night Live” is about to begin its 50th season. Jean Smart will host. The 73-year-old “Hacks” and “Designing Women” star who just won her sixth Emmy has never hosted the sketch comedy institution in her more than 40-year career.</span></a>
    </div>

 data-gtm-topic="No Value" data-align-top data-gtm-region-item >

            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>Usher’s new concert film ‘Usher: Rendezvous in Paris’ is playing in theaters through Sunday. The R&amp;B star sat down with AP entertainment journalist Gary Gerard Hamilton to talk about the significance of his Paris concert and the resulting film, recent online discussion about successors to Michael Jackson, and chasing the success of his “Confessions” album.</p></div>

    <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-body">
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">Zedd’s ‘timeless’ new album ‘Telos’ comes after nine-year wait | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>Nearly a decade after his last full-length release, Zedd is releasing “Telos.” The Grammy-winning producer/DJ says he needed to push himself to make an album that would move the needle — one that told a story beyond the success of his debut LP, “Clarity,” or “True Colors.” The German dance-pop maverick says the album — which features collaborators ranging from Muse and John Mayer to Remi Wolf and Bea Miller — is “an album that for many years I doubted I could create.” He spoke with AP entertainment journalist Rick Taber about the long process of creating “Telos,” being inspired by Jeff Buckley and the state of EDM.</p></div>

        <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-info"><div class="VideoPlaylistItem-info-title">Zedd’s ‘timeless’ new album ‘Telos’ comes after nine-year wait | AP interview</div><div class="VideoPlaylistItem-info-description"><p>Nearly a decade after his last full-length release, Zedd is releasing “Telos.” The Grammy-winning producer/DJ says he needed to push himself to make an album that would move the needle — one that told a story beyond the success of his debut LP, “Clarity,” or “True Colors.” The German dance-pop maverick says the album — which features collaborators ranging from Muse and John Mayer to Remi Wolf and Bea Miller — is “an album that for many years I doubted I could create.” He spoke with AP entertainment journalist Rick Taber about the long process of creating “Telos,” being inspired by Jeff Buckley and the state of EDM.</p></div></div>

            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">Michael Keaton on reuniting with Tim Burton for ‘Beetlejuice Beetlejuice’ | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>Michael Keaton says it would have been a “huge mistake” for his titular trickster ghost character to get significantly more screen time in “Beetlejuice Beetlejuice” than he did in the first film. The 72-year-old star sat down with AP entertainment journalist Gary Gerard Hamilton to talk about why he was nervous to return for the sequel featuring Jenna Ortega and Winona Ryder, the impact of Tim Burton’s original 1988 horror comedy — and why he never thought of himself as playing Batman.</p></div>

        <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-info"><div class="VideoPlaylistItem-info-title">Michael Keaton on reuniting with Tim Burton for ‘Beetlejuice Beetlejuice’ | AP interview</div><div class="VideoPlaylistItem-info-description"><p>Michael Keaton says it would have been a “huge mistake” for his titular trickster ghost character to get significantly more screen time in “Beetlejuice Beetlejuice” than he did in the first film. The 72-year-old star sat down with AP entertainment journalist Gary Gerard Hamilton to talk about why he was nervous to return for the sequel featuring Jenna Ortega and Winona Ryder, the impact of Tim Burton’s original 1988 horror comedy — and why he never thought of himself as playing Batman.</p></div></div>

            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">Justin Baldoni’s ‘It Ends With Us’ journey | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>Justin Baldoni’s “It Ends With Us” journey began well before Colleen Hoover’s novel became a sensation on TikTok. The 40-year-old actor and filmmaker optioned the book in 2019 while he was shooting “Jane The Virgin” and preparing to release his feature film directorial debut, “Five Feet Apart.” Five years later, he spoke with AP entertainment journalist Alicia Rancilio about directing and co-starring alongside Blake Lively in the drama that revolves around domestic violence. </p></div>

            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">Orville Peck’s ‘Stampede’ features stars from country and pop | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>It is not easy to be an outsider in country music, but Orville Peck has made a career out of it. On his third album, “Stampede,” his nonconformist spirit has led to collaborations with everyone from Willie Nelson and Elton John to Mickey Guyton and Kylie Minogue. The 36-year-old South African musician has been steadily stripping back his mask since his 2019 debut album “Pony.” Peck spoke with AP music journalist Maria Sherman about his growing confidence, his high-profile collaborations and country radio.</p></div>

    <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-body">
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">How ‘Trap’ star Josh Hartnett avoided his own Hollywood trap | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>Josh Hartnett is looking back at shedding his Hollywood heartthrob image in the 2000s as he stars in M. Night Shyamalan’s thriller “Trap.” Hartnett is now 46 and lives in England with his wife and four children. While he’s been working steadily since breaking out in 1998 with a “Halloween” sequel and “The Faculty,” he intentionally moved away from studio movies and leading man roles after being typecast as his fame grew with movies like “Black Hawk Down” and “Pearl Harbor.” In “Trap,” Hartnett plays a father with a secret who takes his daughter to a pop concert — which is surrounded by police searching for a serial killer. </p></div>

    <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-body">
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">M. Night Shyamalan’s risky self-financing run continues with ‘Trap’ | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>M. Night Shyamalan has been at least partly self-financing his films since 2015’s “The Visit,” risking his own money on box office success. His latest is “Trap,” starring Josh Hartnett as a father with a secret and Shyamalan’s daughter Saleka as a pop star whose concert is surrounded by police looking to capture a serial killer. Shyamalan spoke with AP entertainment editor Ryan Pearson about his high-risk, high-reward, lower-budget filmmaking approach, guiding his daughters’ artistic pursuits — and his philosophy that “talent is process.”</p></div>

    <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-body">
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">Taika Waititi and Jemaine Clement go their own way for ‘Time Bandits’ series | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>Taika Waititi and Jemaine Clement co-created and play recurring characters in the new Apple TV+ “Time Bandits” series starring Lisa Kudrow. While it’s inspired by Terry Gilliam’s beloved 1981 fantasy film, the two say they mostly went their own way when approaching the story.             <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-title">Glen Powell and Adria Arjona on ‘Hit Man,’ Powell’s dog Brisket, that phone scene | AP interview</div>
        
        
            <div class="VideoPlaylistItem-description"><p>“Hit Man” stars Glen Powell and Adria Arjona downed tequila to break their Dry January pledges together the first time they met. “Life is not about following rules. Powell and Arjona spoke with AP entertainment journalist Ryan Pearson about how they connected off-screen, Linklater’s thorough preparation — and the high-wire cell phone scene that had audiences at festivals applauding mid-screening. “Hit Man” is now in theaters and hits Netflix June 7.</p></div>

	var onCookie = document.cookie
    try {
        var theCookie = onCookie.match(/(OptanonConsent=.*;?)/)[0]
        if (typeof OnetrustActiveGroups === 'string' && OnetrustActiveGroups.split(',').indexOf('4') > 0) {
			var consentId = theCookie.match(/(consentId.*?&)/)[0].replace('&','')
            permutive.consent({"opt_in":true,"token": consentId})
        } else {
            permutive.consent({"opt_in":false})
        }
    } catch(err) {
        console.error('oncookieerror', err)
    }
}</script>
